   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    KDE
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>

      <p>
       <b>
        KDE
       </b>
       (
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">
            ˌ
           </span>
           <span title="'k' in 'kind'">
            k
           </span>
           <span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">
            eɪ
           </span>
           <span title="'d' in 'dye'">
            d
           </span>
           <span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">
            iː
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">
            iː
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       ) is an international
       <a href="/wiki/Free_software" title="Free software">
        free software
       </a>
       community
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       that develops Free and Open Source based software. Well-known products include the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plasma_Desktop" title="Plasma Desktop">
        Plasma Desktop
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/KDE_Frameworks" title="KDE Frameworks">
        KDE Frameworks
       </a>
       and a range of
       <a href="/wiki/Cross-platform" title="Cross-platform">
        cross-platform
       </a>
       applications designed to run on
       <a href="/wiki/Unix-like" title="Unix-like">
        Unix-like
       </a>
       desktops,
       <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">
        Microsoft Windows
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">
        Android
       </a>
       . It further provides tools and documentation for developers that enables them to write software. This supporting role makes KDE a central development hub and home for many popular applications and projects like
       <a href="/wiki/Calligra_Suite" title="Calligra Suite">
        Calligra Suite
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Krita" title="Krita">
        Krita
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/DigiKam" title="DigiKam">
        digiKam
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The Plasma Desktop, being one of the most recognized projects of KDE, is the default
       <a href="/wiki/Desktop_environment" title="Desktop environment">
        desktop environment
       </a>
       on many Linux distributions, such as
       <a href="/wiki/OpenSUSE" title="OpenSUSE">
        openSUSE
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mageia" title="Mageia">
        Mageia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Chakra_(operating_system)" title="Chakra (operating system)">
        Chakra
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kubuntu" title="Kubuntu">
        Kubuntu
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/PCLinuxOS" title="PCLinuxOS">
        PCLinuxOS
       </a>
       . It was also the default desktop environment on
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PC-BSD" title="PC-BSD">
        PC-BSD
       </a>
       , but was later replaced with
       <a href="/wiki/Lumina_(desktop_environment)" title="Lumina (desktop environment)">
        Lumina
       </a>
       , a desktop environment which, like KDE, is written in
       <a href="/wiki/C%2B%2B" title="C++">
        C++
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Qt_(software)" title="Qt (software)">
        Qt
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

          <span class="toctext">
           See also
          </span>
         </a>
        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34">
         <a href="#References">
          <span class="tocnumber">
           11
          </span>
          <span class="toctext">
           References
          </span>
         </a>
        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35">
         <a href="#External_links">

        </li>
       </ul>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">
        Overview
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=KDE&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Overview">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The work of the KDE community can be measured in the following figures:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        KDE is one of the largest active
        <a href="/wiki/Free_software" title="Free software">
         Free Software
        </a>
        communities.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kde-press-page_3-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-kde-press-page-3">
          [3]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        More than 1800 contributors participate in developing KDE software.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kde-press-page_3-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-kde-press-page-3">
          [3]
         </a>
        </sup>
        About 20 new developers contribute their first code each month.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KDE_Reaches_1,000,000_Commits_in_its_Subversion_Repository_4-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-KDE_Reaches_1,000,000_Commits_in_its_Subversion_Repository-4">
          [4]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/KDE_Projects" title="KDE Projects">
         KDE Software
        </a>
        consists of over 6 million lines of code (not including
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qt_(framework)" title="Qt (framework)">
         Qt
        </a>
        ).
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kde-press-page_3-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-kde-press-page-3">
          [3]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        KDE Software is translated in over 108 languages.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
         <a href="#cite_note-5">
          [5]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        KDE Software is available on more than 114 official FTP mirrors in over 34 countries.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
         <a href="#cite_note-6">
          [6]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        A read-only mirror of all repositories can be found on Github.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
         <a href="#cite_note-7">
          [7]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=KDE&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">
        Origins
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=KDE&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Origins">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Matthias_Ettrich_LinuxTag_2005-06-23.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Matthias_Ettrich_LinuxTag_2005-06-23.jpg/220px-Matthias_Ettrich_LinuxTag_2005-06-23.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Matthias_Ettrich_LinuxTag_2005-06-23.jpg/330px-Matthias_Ettrich_LinuxTag_2005-06-23.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Matthias_Ettrich_LinuxTag_2005-06-23.jpg/440px-Matthias_Ettrich_LinuxTag_2005-06-23.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Matthias_Ettrich_LinuxTag_2005-06-23.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Matthias_Ettrich" title="Matthias Ettrich">
          Matthias Ettrich
         </a>
         , Founder of KDE
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       K Desktop Environment (KDE) was founded in 1996 by
       <a href="/wiki/Matthias_Ettrich" title="Matthias Ettrich">
        Matthias Ettrich
       </a>
       , who was then a student at the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eberhard_Karls_University_of_T%C3%BCbingen" title="Eberhard Karls University of Tübingen">
        Eberhard Karls University of Tübingen
       </a>
       . At the time, he was troubled by certain aspects of the
       <a href="/wiki/Unix" title="Unix">
        Unix
       </a>
       desktop. Among his concerns was that none of the
       <a href="/wiki/Application_software" title="Application software">
        applications
       </a>
       looked, felt, or worked alike. He proposed the creation of not merely a set of applications but a desktop environment in which users could expect things to look, feel, and work consistently. He also wanted to make this desktop easy to use; one of his complaints about desktop applications of the time was that it is too complicated for end user. His initial
       <a href="/wiki/Usenet" title="Usenet">
        Usenet
       </a>
       post spurred a lot of interest, and the KDE project was born.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_Project:_Kool_Desktop_Environment_(KDE)_8-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-New_Project:_Kool_Desktop_Environment_(KDE)-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The name
       <i>
        KDE
       </i>
       was intended as a wordplay on the existing
       <a href="/wiki/Common_Desktop_Environment" title="Common Desktop Environment">
        Common Desktop Environment
       </a>
       , available for Unix systems. CDE was an X11-based user environment jointly developed by HP, IBM, and Sun through the
       <a href="/wiki/X/Open" title="X/Open">
        X/Open
       </a>
       consortium, with an interface and productivity tools based on the
       <a href="/wiki/Motif_(software)" title="Motif (software)">
        Motif
       </a>
       graphical
       <a href="/wiki/Widget_toolkit" title="Widget toolkit">
        widget toolkit
       </a>
       . It was supposed to be an intuitively easy-to-use desktop computer environment.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <i>
        K
       </i>
       was originally suggested to stand for "
       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/kool" title="wikt:kool">
        Kool
       </a>
       ", but it was quickly decided that the K should stand for nothing in particular. Therefore, the
       <i>
        KDE
       </i>
       initialism expanded to
       <i>
        "K Desktop Environment"
       </i>
       before it was dropped altogether in favor of KDE = Community due to the rebranding effort.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Brand_repositioning">
        Brand repositioning
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=KDE&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Brand repositioning">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       On 24 November 2009 the KDE Marketing Team announced a
       <a href="/wiki/Rebranding" title="Rebranding">
        rebranding
       </a>
       of the KDE project components, motivated by the perceived shift from building a desktop environment to a wider ranging project around a community of "people who create software". The rebranding focused on de-emphasizing the desktop environment as "just another product", and emphasizing both the community and the other technologies provided as KDE software. What would have been previously known as KDE 4 was split into three products: Plasma Workspaces, KDE Applications, and KDE Platform – bundled as "KDE Software Compilation 4" (abbreviated "KDE SC 4").
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As of today the name
       <i>
        KDE
       </i>
       no longer stands for
       <i>
        K Desktop Environment
       </i>
       , but for the community that produces the software.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Community_structure">
        Community structure
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=KDE&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Community structure">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mascot">
        Mascot
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=KDE&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Mascot">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:KDE_Mascot_Konqi_by_Tyson_Tan.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3470" data-file-width="2082" height="367" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/KDE_Mascot_Konqi_by_Tyson_Tan.png/220px-KDE_Mascot_Konqi_by_Tyson_Tan.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/KDE_Mascot_Konqi_by_Tyson_Tan.png/330px-KDE_Mascot_Konqi_by_Tyson_Tan.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/KDE_Mascot_Konqi_by_Tyson_Tan.png/440px-KDE_Mascot_Konqi_by_Tyson_Tan.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:KDE_Mascot_Konqi_by_Tyson_Tan.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Konqi
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Konqi" title="Konqi">
        Konqi
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The KDE community’s
       <a href="/wiki/Mascot" title="Mascot">
        mascot
       </a>
       is a green dragon named
       <a href="/wiki/Konqi" title="Konqi">
        Konqi
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Konqi has a girlfriend named Katie. Konqi and Katie made their costumed appearance at the KDE 4.0 Release Event and Camp KDE 2010.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Konqi also appears on the KDE software's about dialog.
       <a href="/wiki/Konqi#Kandalf" title="Konqi">
        Kandalf the wizard
       </a>
       was the former mascot for the KDE community during its 1.x and 2.x versions, but he was dropped owing to copyright issues (his resemblance to
       <a href="/wiki/Gandalf" title="Gandalf">
        Gandalf
       </a>
       ). Konqi's appearance was officially redesigned with the coming of Plasma 5, with
       <a href="/wiki/Tyson_Tan" title="Tyson Tan">
        Tyson Tan
       </a>
       's entry (seen on the right) winning the redesign competition on the KDE Forums.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Organization">
        Organization
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=KDE&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Organization">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The financial and legal matters of KDE are handled by
       <a href="/wiki/KDE_e.V." title="KDE e.V.">
        KDE e.V.
       </a>
       , a German non-profit organization that has its seat in Berlin. The organization also assists the community members in organizing their conferences and meetings.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       KDE e.V. helps run the servers needed by the KDE community. It owns the
       <a href="/wiki/Trademark" title="Trademark">
        trademark
       </a>
       <i>
        KDE
       </i>
       and the corresponding logo. It pays for travel costs to meetings and subsidizes events.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Working groups that are formed are designed to formalize some roles within KDE, and to improve coordination within KDE as well as communication between the various parts of KDE.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       KDE e.V. does not influence software development. The logo of KDE e.V. was contributed by
       <a href="/wiki/David_Vignoni" title="David Vignoni">
        David Vignoni
       </a>
       . The three flags on top of the logo represent the three main tasks of KDE e.V.: supporting the community, representing the community, and governing the community.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The KDE community's developer meetings, servers, and related events are frequently
       <a href="/wiki/Sponsor_(commercial)" title="Sponsor (commercial)">
        sponsored
       </a>
       by individuals, universities, and businesses.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <i>
        supporting members
       </i>
       of the KDE e.V. are extraordinary members supporting the KDE through financial or material contributions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Supporting members are entitled to display the
       <i>
        "Member of KDE"
       </i>
       logo on their website or in printed materials. The
       <i>
        Patron of KDE
       </i>
       is the highest level of supporting member. The patrons of KDE also are entitled to display the exclusive
       <i>
        "Patron of KDE"
       </i>
       logo on their website or in printed materials.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On 15 October 2006, it was announced that
       <a href="/wiki/Mark_Shuttleworth" title="Mark Shuttleworth">
        Mark Shuttleworth
       </a>
       had become the first
       <i>
        Patron of KDE
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kdepatron_22-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-kdepatron-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On 7 July 2007, it was announced that Intel Corporation and Novell had also become patrons of KDE.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In January 2010, Google became a supporting member. On 9 June 2010, KDE e.V. launched the "Join the Game" campaign. This campaign promotes the idea of becoming a supporting member for individuals. It is made available for those who would like to support KDE, but do not have enough time to do so.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Georg_Greve" title="Georg Greve">
        Georg Greve
       </a>
       , founder of the
       <a href="/wiki/Free_Software_Foundation_Europe" title="Free Software Foundation Europe">
        Free Software Foundation Europe
       </a>
       (FSFE) was first to 'join the game'.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Local_community">
        Local community
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=KDE&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Local community">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In many countries, KDE has local branches. These are either informal organizations (KDE India) or like the KDE e.V., given a legal form (KDE France). The local organizations host and maintain regional websites, and organise local events, such as tradeshows, contributor meetings and social community meetings.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:82px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:KDE-AR_Official_Logo.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="97" data-file-width="95" height="82" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/KDE-AR_Official_Logo.png/80px-KDE-AR_Official_Logo.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/15/KDE-AR_Official_Logo.png 1.5x" width="80"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:KDE-AR_Official_Logo.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         KDE–AR logo
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       KDE–AR (KDE Argentina) is the group of KDE developers and users in Argentina, and was officially opened on November 22, 2008 at a meeting in an IRC channel. They organise release parties on holidays to celebrate releases of new versions of the KDE SC since 4.2. KDE–AR has an own mailing lists and an IRC channel.
      </p>
      <p>
       KDE Brasil is composed by several local groups in Brazil, like KDE–MG, Live Blue, KDE Piauí, and KDE–RS. The main goals of local groups are regional promotion and direction of contributions of members, and still maintaining harmony with the KDE Brazil community. KDE–MG is a local group in
       <a href="/wiki/Minas_Gerais" title="Minas Gerais">
        Minas Gerais
       </a>
       . The idea of structuring the group has arisen during the FISL (Fórum Internacional Software Livre) 10. Live Blue is a KDE working group in
       <a href="/wiki/Bahia" title="Bahia">
        Bahia
       </a>
       . KDE Piauí is a group of users and contributors of KDE in the
       <a href="/wiki/Piau%C3%AD" title="Piauí">
        Piauí
       </a>
       . The idea was born during the Software Freedom Day Teresina 2009 and has concretized during the Akademy–Br 2010, where the group was officially created. KDE–RS is a group of KDE users from
       <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande_do_Sul" title="Rio Grande do Sul">
        Rio Grande do Sul
       </a>
       . KDE Lovelace is a Brazilian female group of users and contributors in KDE.
      </p>
      <p>
       KDE España was registered as an association under the Spanish law in 2009. The aim is stimulating the development and use of the KDE software in Spain. Its supreme governing body is the general assembly. Ordinary as well as extraordinary general assemblies can be held. An ordinary general assembly is held at least once a year. Extraordinary general assemblies are held as necessary. The board consists of the president, the vice president, the secretary, the treasurer and members. In the current board are Aleix Pol i Gonzàlez (president), Alejandro Fiestas Olivares (vice president), Víctor Blázquez Francisco (secretary), and José Millán Soto (treasurer).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In addition, KDE España is the official representative of KDE e.V. in Spain.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       KDE.in (KDE India), founded in 2005, provides Indian KDE developers and users with a community hub to coordinate with and support each other. Besides making efforts in the internationalization and localization, a major aim is to foster the creation and adaptation of KDE applications to needs specific to India.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Japan KDE Users' Group
       <span style="font-weight: normal">
        (
        <span lang="ja">
         JKUG/日本 KDE ユーザ会
        </span>
        <span style="display:none">
         ,
        </span>
        <i>
         Nihon KDE Yūzakai
        </i>
        )
       </span>
       is the Japanese local users' group of KDE. The membership types of the association are corporate members
       <span style="font-weight: normal">
        (
        <span lang="ja">
         法人会員
        </span>
        <span style="display:none">
         ,
        </span>
        <i>
         hōjin kaiin
        </i>
        )
       </span>
       and individual members
       <span style="font-weight: normal">
        (
        <span lang="ja">
         個人会員
        </span>
        <span style="display:none">
         ,
        </span>
        <i>
         kojin kaiin
        </i>
        )
       </span>
       . About 15 members form the active staff. The officers include one president
       <span style="font-weight: normal">
        (
        <span lang="ja">
         会長
        </span>
        <span style="display:none">
         ,
        </span>
        <i>
         kaichō
        </i>
        )
       </span>
       , two vice presidents
       <span style="font-weight: normal">
        (
        <span lang="ja">
         副会長
        </span>
        <span style="display:none">
         ,
        </span>
        <i>
         fuku-kaichō
        </i>
        )
       </span>
       and one accountant. Currently, president is Daisuke Kameda
       <span style="font-weight: normal">
        (
        <span lang="ja">
         亀田大輔
        </span>
        <span style="display:none">
         ,
        </span>
        <i>
         Kameda Daisuke
        </i>
        )
       </span>
       , vice presidents are Taiki Komoda
       <span style="font-weight: normal">
        (
        <span lang="ja">
         菰田泰生
        </span>
        <span style="display:none">
         ,
        </span>
        <i>
         Komoda Taiki
        </i>
        )
       </span>
       and Satoru Satō
       <span style="font-weight: normal">
        (
        <span lang="ja">
         佐藤暁
        </span>
        <span style="display:none">
         ,
        </span>
        <i>
         Satō Satoru
        </i>
        )
       </span>
       . The association holds an annual general assembly in December.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Its activities include message translation to Japanese, making patches for multilingualization, and exchanging information about KDE/Qt.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       KDE GB is a KDE community with a constitution in Britain. At their meeting in October 2010 they agreed to register as a charity.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       KDE-ir (فارسی KDE) is a Persian KDE community. Korean KDE Users Group was started in 1999. The group's work is mostly translation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       KDE România is a community founded in Romania in 2013.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Communication">
        Communication
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=KDE&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Communication">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:KDE_mascot_Konqi_for_help_and_other_documentations.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3686" data-file-width="3508" height="231" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/KDE_mascot_Konqi_for_help_and_other_documentations.png/220px-KDE_mascot_Konqi_for_help_and_other_documentations.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/KDE_mascot_Konqi_for_help_and_other_documentations.png/330px-KDE_mascot_Konqi_for_help_and_other_documentations.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/KDE_mascot_Konqi_for_help_and_other_documentations.png/440px-KDE_mascot_Konqi_for_help_and_other_documentations.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:KDE_mascot_Konqi_for_help_and_other_documentations.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         KDE mascot
         <a href="/wiki/Konqi" title="Konqi">
          Konqi
         </a>
         managing documentations.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Communication within the community takes place via mailing lists, IRC, blogs, forums, news announcements,
       <a href="/wiki/Wiki" title="Wiki">
        wikis
       </a>
       and conferences. The community has a
       <i>
        Code of Conduct
       </i>
       for acceptable behavior within the community.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Mailing_list" title="Mailing list">
        mailing lists
       </a>
       are one of the main channels of communication. The
       <i>
        Kde
       </i>
       list is for user discussion and
       <i>
        Kde-announce
       </i>
       for version updates, security patches and other changes. The general development lists are
       <i>
        Kde-devel
       </i>
       , for developer communication, and
       <i>
        Kde-core-devel
       </i>
       , used to discuss development of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KDE_Platform" title="KDE Platform">
        KDE Platform
       </a>
       . Many applications have individual mailing lists.
      </p>
      <p>
       The KDE Community Forums are actively used. "KDE Brainstorm", allows users to submit ideas to developers. The request can then be considered by other users. Every few months, the highest-voted features are submitted to developers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       IRC bots that announce new threads and posts on IRC channels, by braiding forum posts into mailinglist messages and by offering RSS feeds.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       KDE has three wikis: UserBase, TechBase and Community Wiki. They are translated with the
       <a href="/wiki/Translatewiki.net" title="Translatewiki.net">
        MediaWiki Translate extension
       </a>
       . UserBase provides documentation for end users: tutorials, links to help and an application catalogue. Its logo was designed by Eugene Trounev.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       TechBase provides technical documentation for developers and system administrators.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Community Wiki coordinates community teams. It is used for publishing and sharing community-internal information.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Internet_Relay_Chat" title="Internet Relay Chat">
        IRC
       </a>
       channels provide real-time discussions. Planet KDE is made from the blogs of KDE's contributors.
       <a href="/wiki/KDE_Dot_News" title="KDE Dot News">
        KDE.News
       </a>
       is the website of office news announcements.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       KDE Buzz tracks identi.ca, Twitter, Picasa, Flickr and YouTube to show social media activity concerning KDE.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       KDE Pastebin allows for posting of source code snippets and provides
       <a href="/wiki/Syntax_highlighting" title="Syntax highlighting">
        syntax highlighting
       </a>
       to ease reviewing code. Sections can be password protected. RSS notifies of new posts.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       KDE Bug Tracking System uses
       <a href="/wiki/Bugzilla" title="Bugzilla">
        Bugzilla
       </a>
       to manage reports and fixes. "Behind KDE" offers interviews with KDE contributors.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Identity">
        Identity
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=KDE&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Identity">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       KDE has community identity guidelines (CIG) for definitions and recommendations which help the community to establish a unique, characteristic, and appealing design.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The KDE official logo displays the white trademarked K-Gear shape on a blue square with mitred corners. Copying of the KDE Logo is subject to the LGPL.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Some local community logos are derivations of the official logo. The KDE software labels are used by producers of software to show that they are part of the KDE community or that they use the KDE Platform. There are three labels available. The
       <i>
        Powered by KDE
       </i>
       label is used to show that an application derives its strength from the KDE community and from the KDE development platform. The
       <i>
        Built on the KDE Platform
       </i>
       label indicates that the application uses the KDE platform. The
       <i>
        Part of the KDE family
       </i>
       label is used by application authors to identify themselves as being part of the KDE community.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Many KDE applications have a
       <i>
        K
       </i>
       in the name, mostly as an initial letter. The
       <i>
        K
       </i>
       in many KDE applications is obtained by spelling a word which originally begins with
       <i>
        C
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        Q
       </i>
       differently, for example
       <a href="/wiki/Konsole" title="Konsole">
        Konsole
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Kaffeine" title="Kaffeine">
        Kaffeine
       </a>
       . Also, some just prefix a commonly used word with a
       <i>
        K
       </i>
       , for instance
       <a href="/wiki/KGet" title="KGet">
        KGet
       </a>
       . Among KDE SC 4 applications and technologies, however, the trend is not to have a
       <i>
        K
       </i>
       in the name at all, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Calligra_Stage" title="Calligra Stage">
        Stage
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dolphin_(software)" title="Dolphin (software)">
        Dolphin
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Contributors">
        Contributors
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=KDE&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Contributors">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Like many free/open source projects, developing KDE software is primarily a volunteer effort, although various companies, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Novell" title="Novell">
        Novell
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nokia" title="Nokia">
        Nokia
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Blue_Systems" title="Blue Systems">
        Blue Systems
       </a>
       employ or employed developers to work on various parts of the project. Since a large number of individuals contribute to KDE in various ways (e.g. code, translation, artwork), organization of such a project is complex.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Development">
        Development
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=KDE&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Development">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The overall direction of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KDE_Platform" title="KDE Platform">
        KDE Platform
       </a>
       is made by the
       <i>
        KDE Core Team
       </i>
       . These are developers who have made significant contributions within KDE over a long period of time. This team communicates using the
       <i>
        kde-core-devel
       </i>
       mailing list, which is publicly archived and readable, but joining requires approval. KDE does not have a single central leader who can veto important decisions. Instead, the KDE core team consisting of several dozen contributors taking decisions. The decisions do not take a formal vote, but through discussions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Developers also organize alongside topical teams. For example, the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/KDE_Education_Project" title="KDE Education Project">
         KDE Edu team
        </a>
       </i>
       develops free educational software. While these teams work mostly independent and do not all follow a common release schedule. Each team has its own messaging channels, both on IRC and on the mailinglists. And they have mentor program which helps beginners to get started.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Currently the KDE community uses the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Git_(software)" title="Git (software)">
        Git
       </a>
       revision control system. The KDE Projects site and QuickGit give an overview of all projects hosted by KDE's Git repository system.
       <a href="/wiki/Review_Board" title="Review Board">
        Review Board
       </a>
       is used for patch review.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2012)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Commitfilter will send an email with each commit for the projects you want to watch, without either getting tons of mails or getting infrequent and redundant information. English Breakfast Network (EBN) is a collection of machines that do automated KDE source artifact quality checking. The EBN provides KDE
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/API" title="API">
        API
       </a>
       documentation validation, user documentation validation, source code checking. It is operated by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adriaan_de_Groot_(Software_developer)" title="Adriaan de Groot (Software developer)">
        Adriaan de Groot
       </a>
       and Allen Winter. Commit-Digest site gives a weekly overview of the development activity. LXR indexes classes and methods used in KDE.
      </p>
      <p>
       Season of KDE (SoK) is a program for people who could not get accepted into Google Summer of Code. They will have a mentor from the KDE community to help them if any question arises or if they do not know how to continue.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Season_of_KDE_47-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Season_of_KDE-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 20 July 2009, KDE announced that the one millionth commit has been made to its Subversion repository.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KDE_Reaches_1,000,000_Commits_in_its_Subversion_Repository_4-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-KDE_Reaches_1,000,000_Commits_in_its_Subversion_Repository-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On October 11, 2009,
       <a href="/wiki/Cornelius_Schumacher" title="Cornelius Schumacher">
        Cornelius Schumacher
       </a>
       , a main developer within KDE,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       wrote about the estimated cost (using the
       <a href="/wiki/COCOMO" title="COCOMO">
        COCOMO
       </a>
       model with SLOCCount) to develop KDE software package with 4,273,291
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lines_of_Code" title="Lines of Code">
        LoC
       </a>
       , which would be about US$175,364,716.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This estimation does not include Qt,
       <a href="/wiki/Calligra_Suite" title="Calligra Suite">
        Calligra Suite
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Amarok_(software)" title="Amarok (software)">
        Amarok
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Digikam" title="Digikam">
        Digikam
       </a>
       , and other applications that are not part of KDE core.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (April 2012)">
           clarification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_groups">
        Other groups
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=KDE&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Other groups">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The KDE community has many smaller teams working towards specific goals. The
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KDE_Accessibility_Project" title="KDE Accessibility Project">
         Accessibility team
        </a>
       </i>
       make KDE accessible to all users, including those with physical handicaps.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <i>
        Artists team
       </i>
       has designed most of the artwork used by the software like icons, wallpapers and themes. They have also produced graphics for T-shirts and websites. Discussions of the team is most active on the IRC channel.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <i>
        Bugsquad team
       </i>
       keeps track of incoming bugs. They verify that a bug exists, that it is reproducible, and that the reporter has given enough information. The goal is to help developers notice valid bugs quicker, and to save their time.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <i>
        Documentation team
       </i>
       writes documentation for applications.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The team uses the
       <a href="/wiki/DocBook" title="DocBook">
        DocBook
       </a>
       format and custom tools to create documentation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <i>
        Localization team
       </i>
       translates KDE software into many different languages. This team works beside the Documentation team.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <i>
        Marketing and Promotion team
       </i>
       manages marketing and promotion. The team writes news articles, release announcements and other webpages on KDE websites. The articles of KDE.News is submitted by the team. It also has channels at social media sites for communication and promotion. They also attend conference events.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <i>
        Research team
       </i>
       is to improve the collaboration with external parties to achieve more funded research. They support community members by providing information, navigating bureaucracies, and matching research partners. The
       <i>
        usability team
       </i>
       has written a
       <a href="/wiki/Human_interface_guidelines" title="Human interface guidelines">
        Human Interface Guideline
       </a>
       (HIG) for the developers and they do regular reviews of KDE applications. The HIG provides a standardized layout.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <i>
        Web team
       </i>
       maintains KDE’s web presence. The
       <i>
        KDE Women
       </i>
       help women to contribute and encourage women to give talks at conferences.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <i>
        Release team
       </i>
       defines and executes the official software releases. The Team is responsible for setting release schedules for the official releases. This includes release dates, deadlines for individual release steps and restrictions for code changes. The Release Team coordinates release dates with the marketing and press efforts of KDE. The release team is composed of Module Coordinators, Marketing Team liaison, and the people who actually do the work of tagging and creating the releases.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Activities">
        Activities
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=KDE&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Activities">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The two most important conferences of KDE are
       <i>
        Akademy
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        Camp KDE
       </i>
       . Each event is on a large scale, both thematically and geographically.
       <i>
        Akademy-BR
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        Akademy-es
       </i>
       are local community events.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Akademy">
        Akademy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=KDE&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Akademy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Akademy_2008_logo.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="272" data-file-width="484" height="84" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Akademy_2008_logo.png/150px-Akademy_2008_logo.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Akademy_2008_logo.png/225px-Akademy_2008_logo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Akademy_2008_logo.png/300px-Akademy_2008_logo.png 2x" width="150"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Akademy_2008_logo.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Akademy 2008 logo
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Akademy" title="Akademy">
         Akademy
        </a>
       </i>
       is the annual world summit, held each summer at varying venues in Europe.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The primary goals of Akademy are to act as a community building event, to communicate the achievements of community, and to provide a platform for collaboration with community and industry partners. Secondary goals are to engage local people, and to provide space for getting together to write code.
       <a href="/wiki/KDE_e.V." title="KDE e.V.">
        KDE e.V.
       </a>
       assist with procedures, advice and organization. Akademy including conference, KDE e.V. general assembly, marathon coding sessions, BOFs (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Birds_of_a_Feather_(computing)" title="Birds of a Feather (computing)">
        birds of a feather
       </a>
       sessions) and social program. BOFs are meet to discuss specific sub-projects or issues.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The KDE community held KDE One that was first conference in
       <a href="/wiki/Arnsberg" title="Arnsberg">
        Arnsberg
       </a>
       , Germany in 1997 to discuss the first KDE release. Initially, each conference was numbered after the release, and not regular held. Since 2003 the conferences were held once a year. And they were named Akademy since 2004.
      </p>
      <p>
       The yearly Akademy conference gives
       <i>
        Akademy Awards
       </i>
       , are awards that the KDE community gives to KDE contributors. Their purpose is to recognize outstanding contribution to KDE. There are three awards, best application, best non-application and jury's award. As always the winners are chosen by the winners from the previous year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       First winners received a framed picture of
       <a href="/wiki/Konqi" title="Konqi">
        Konqi
       </a>
       signed by all attending KDE developers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Camp_KDE">
        Camp KDE
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=KDE&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Camp KDE">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="wikitable" style="float:right;">
       <tr style="background:#efefef;">
        <th>
         Year
        </th>
        <th>
         Venue
        </th>

        </th>

         <a href="/wiki/Negril" title="Negril">

         </a>

         <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">

         1/17–1/18
        </td>

       <tr>
        <th>

        </th>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/La_Jolla" title="La Jolla">
          La Jolla
         </a>
         , United States
        </td>

      <p>
       <i>
        Camp KDE
       </i>
       is another annual contributor’s conference of the KDE community. The event provides a regional opportunity for contributors and enthusiasts to gather and share their experiences. It is free to all participants. It is intended to ensure that KDE in the world is not simply seen as being Euro-centric. The KDE e.V. helps travel and accommodation subsidies for presenters, BoF leaders, organizers or core contributor. It is held in the North America since 2009.
      </p>
      <p>
       In January 2008, KDE 4.0 Release Event was held at the Google headquarters in Mountain View, California, USA to celebrate the release of KDE SC 4.0. The community realized that there was a strong demand for KDE events in the Americas, therefore Camp KDE was produced.
      </p>
      <p>
       Camp KDE 2009 was the premiere meeting of the KDE Americas, was held at the Travellers Beach Resort in Negril, Jamaica, sponsored by Google, Intel, iXsystem, KDE e.V. and Kitware. The event included 1–2 days of presentations, BoF meetings and
       <a href="/wiki/Hackathon" title="Hackathon">
        hackathon
       </a>
       sessions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Camp KDE 2010 took place at the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_San_Diego" title="University of California, San Diego">
        University of California, San Diego
       </a>
       (UCSD) in La Jolla, USA. The schedule included presentations, BoFs, hackathons and a day trip. It started with a short introduction by Jeff Mitchell, who was the principal organizer of the conference, talked a bit of history about Camp KDE and some statistics about the KDE community. The talks of the event were relatively well attended, and an increase over the previous year to around 70 people. On 1/19, the social event was a tour of a local brewery.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Camp KDE 2011 was held at Hotel Kabuki in San Francisco, USA, was co-located with the Linux Foundation Collaboration Summit. The schedule included presentations, hackathons and a party at Noisebridge. The conference opened with an introduction spoken by
       <a href="/wiki/Celeste_Lyn_Paul" title="Celeste Lyn Paul">
        Celeste Lyn Paul
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      <p>
       <i>
        Akademy-es
       </i>
       is a conference for Spanish community since 2006, aimed at Spanish speakers. The event is organized by Spanish local organization.
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=KDE_Espa%C3%B1a&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="KDE España (page does not exist)">
        KDE España
       </a>
       organizes the event since 2008. The annual
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=KDE_Espa%C3%B1a&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="KDE España (page does not exist)">
        KDE España
       </a>
       Assembly takes place during the event.
      </p>
      <p>
       Akademy-es 2006 was held at Espai Jove Bocanord in Barcelona, organized by Badopi.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Akademy-es 2007 was hosted by Hispalinux, Wireless Zaragoza, and the Zaragoza council.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
        <a href="#cite_note-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Akademy-es 2008 was held at
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_A_Coru%C3%B1a" title="University of A Coruña">
        University of A Coruña
       </a>
       , was organized by the KDE España and GPUL, sponsored by Oficina de Software Libre da
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universidade_da_Coru%C3%B1a" title="Universidade da Coruña">
        Universidade da Coruña
       </a>
       , Mancomun,
       <a href="/wiki/Igalia" title="Igalia">
        Igalia
       </a>
       , Qt Software and eyeOs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
        <a href="#cite_note-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Akademy-es 2009 was held in the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Las_Palmas_de_Gran_Canaria" title="University of Las Palmas de Gran Canaria">
        University of Las Palmas de Gran Canaria
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Akademy-es 2010 was held in the Engineering Technical School of Bilbao, was organized by KDE España and Itsas. There were approximately 80 participants. The KDE España Assembly elected the new board consists of Albert Astals Cid (president), Rafael Fernández López (vice president), Aleix Pol (secretary), and José Millán Soto (treasurer).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
        <a href="#cite_note-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Akademy-es 2011 was organized by KDE España, was sponsored by Google and Nokia, and was supported by the Linux and Todo-Linux magazines. The event was held in two different locations: the Polytechnic University of Catalunya for presentations of first day, The School of Sant Marc de Sarrià for last two day.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

       <a class="external text" href="http://conf.KDE.in" rel="nofollow">

       <a href="/wiki/R.V._College_of_Engineering" title="R.V. College of Engineering">
        R.V. College of Engineering
       </a>
       in Bangalore, India. The first three days of the event had talks, tutorials and interactive sessions. The last two days were a focused code sprint.

        </a>

The Lighting of the Auspicious Lamp ceremony was performed to open the conference. The first session was by Lydia Pintscher who talk "So much to do – so little time". At the event, Project Neon announced return on Mar 11, 2011, provides nightly builds of the KDE Software Compilation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
        <a href="#cite_note-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Closing the conference was keynote speaker and old-time KDE developer Sirtaj.

      <p>
       <i>
        Día KDE
       </i>
       (KDE Day) is an Argentinian event focused on KDE. It gives talks and workshops. The purpose of the event are: spread the free software movement among the population of Argentina, bringing to it the KDE community and environment developed by it, to know and strengthen KDE-AR, and generally bring the community together to have fun. The event is free.

         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>

       A
       <i>
        Release party
       </i>
       is a party, which celebrates the release of a new version of the KDE SC (twice a year).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
       KDE also participates in other conferences that revolve around free software.
