      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="KDE_Software">
        KDE Software
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=KDE&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: KDE Software">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KDE_Software" title="KDE Software">
        KDE Software
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Release_Overview">
        Release Overview
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=KDE&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Release Overview">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="wikitable">
       <tr>
        <th>
         Version
        </th>
        <th>
         Date
        </th>
        <th>
         Information
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th>
        </th>
        <td>
         October 14, 1996
        </td>
        <td>
         KDE development announced
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td style="background:#DCDCDC">
         <b>
          1.0
         </b>
        </td>
        <td>
         July 12, 1998
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td style="background:#DCDCDC">
         <b>
          2.0
         </b>
        </td>
        <td>
         October 23, 2000
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td style="background:#DCDCDC">
         <b>
          3.0
         </b>
        </td>
        <td>
         April 3, 2002
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td style="background:#DCDCDC">
         <b>
          <a href="/wiki/KDE_Plasma_4" title="KDE Plasma 4">
           4.0
          </a>
         </b>
        </td>
        <td>
         January 11, 2008
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <b>
          <a href="/wiki/KDE_Plasma_5" title="KDE Plasma 5">
           post-4 series
          </a>
         </b>
        </td>
        <td>
         July 15, 2014
        </td>
        <td>
         former KDE/KDE SC split into KDE Plasma, KDE Frameworks and KDE Applications
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:KDE_4.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1280" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/KDE_4.png/220px-KDE_4.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/KDE_4.png/330px-KDE_4.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/KDE_4.png/440px-KDE_4.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:KDE_4.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         KDE Plasma Desktop 4.10, showing KWrite
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the beginning, Matthias Ettrich chose to use
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trolltech" title="Trolltech">
        Trolltech’s
       </a>
       Qt framework for the KDE project.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
        <a href="#cite_note-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Other programmers quickly started developing KDE/Qt applications, and by early 1997, a few applications were being released. On 12 July 1998 the first version of the desktop environment, called KDE 1.0, was released. The original
       <a href="/wiki/GNU_General_Public_License" title="GNU General Public License">
        GPL
       </a>
       licensed version of this toolkit only existed for platforms which used the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/X11" title="X11">
        X11
       </a>
       display server, but with the release of Qt 4,
       <a href="/wiki/GNU_Lesser_General_Public_License" title="GNU Lesser General Public License">
        LGPL
       </a>
       licensed versions are available for more platforms. This allowed KDE software based on Qt 4 or newer versions to theoretically be distributed to Microsoft Windows and OS X.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
        <a href="#cite_note-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After the switch to Qt5, the core software that was formerly referred to as
       <i>
        KDE
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        KDE SC
       </i>
       now consists of three parts:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        KDE Plasma (providing different workspaces)
       </li>
       <li>
        KDE Frameworks (libraries on top of Qt, formerly known as 'kdelibs' or 'KDE Platform')
       </li>
       <li>
        and KDE Applications.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="KDE_Plasma">
        KDE Plasma
        <span id="Plasma_Workspaces">
        </span>
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=KDE&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: KDE Plasma">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/KDE_Plasma_4" title="KDE Plasma 4">
        KDE Plasma 4
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/KDE_Plasma_5" title="KDE Plasma 5">
        KDE Plasma 5
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Screenshot_of_KDE_4.4_plasma-netbook.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1366" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Screenshot_of_KDE_4.4_plasma-netbook.png/220px-Screenshot_of_KDE_4.4_plasma-netbook.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Screenshot_of_KDE_4.4_plasma-netbook.png/330px-Screenshot_of_KDE_4.4_plasma-netbook.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Screenshot_of_KDE_4.4_plasma-netbook.png/440px-Screenshot_of_KDE_4.4_plasma-netbook.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Screenshot_of_KDE_4.4_plasma-netbook.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         KDE Plasma Netbook
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       KDE Plasma provides a unified environment for running and managing applications on different form factors like desktops, netbooks, tablets or smartphones.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
        <a href="#cite_note-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/KDE_Plasma_4" title="KDE Plasma 4">
        Plasma
       </a>
       first was introduced as part of the KDE4 SC, the fourth generation of
       <a href="/wiki/Desktop_environment" title="Desktop environment">
        graphical environments
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Its successor
       <a href="/wiki/KDE_Plasma_5" title="KDE Plasma 5">
        KDE Plasma 5
       </a>
       was released on July 15, 2014 and currently features the following workspaces:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <i>
         Plasma Desktop
        </i>
        for desktops
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         Plasma Netbook
        </i>
        for netbooks
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         Plasma Media Center
        </i>
        for TVs and set-top boxes
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         Plasma Active
        </i>
        for tablets
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
         <a href="#cite_note-81">
          [81]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plasma_Mobile" title="Plasma Mobile">
          Plasma Mobile
         </a>
        </i>
        for smartphones and general touch-enabled devices
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="KDE_Frameworks">
        KDE Frameworks
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=KDE&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: KDE Frameworks">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/KDE_Platform_4" title="KDE Platform 4">
        KDE Platform 4
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KDE_Frameworks_5" title="KDE Frameworks 5">
        KDE Frameworks 5
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the KDE4 SC series, the
       <a href="/wiki/KDE_Platform_4" title="KDE Platform 4">
        KDE Platform
       </a>
       consisted of the libraries and services needed to run KDE applications. When switching to Qt 5, KDE platform was transformed into a modular set of what is now referred to as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KDE_Frameworks_5" title="KDE Frameworks 5">
        KDE Frameworks
       </a>
       . Libraries include:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solid_(KDE)" title="Solid (KDE)">
        Solid
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NEPOMUK_(framework)" title="NEPOMUK (framework)">
        Nepomuk
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phonon_(KDE)" title="Phonon (KDE)">
        Phonon
       </a>
       , etc. and must be licensed under one of the LGPL, BSD license,
       <a href="/wiki/MIT_License" title="MIT License">
        MIT License
       </a>
       and X11 license.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
        <a href="#cite_note-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       While KDE Frameworks is mainly written in C++, it includes bindings for other programming languages.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Bindings use the following generic technologies:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Smoke: for creating bindings for
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ruby_programming_language" title="Ruby programming language">
         Ruby
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/C_Sharp_(programming_language)" title="C Sharp (programming language)">
         C#
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/PHP" title="PHP">
         PHP
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        SIP: for creating bindings for
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Python_programming_language" title="Python programming language">
         Python
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Kross: Embedded scripting for C++ applications, with support for Ruby, Python, JavaScript,
        <a href="/wiki/QtScript" title="QtScript">
         QtScript
        </a>
        , Falcon and Java
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Stable and mature bindings available for the following programming languages:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
        <a href="#cite_note-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Python
       </li>
       <li>
        Ruby (
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Korundum" title="Korundum">
         Korundum
        </a>
        , built on top of
        <a href="/wiki/QtRuby" title="QtRuby">
         QtRuby
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        C# (However, the current framework for binding to C# and other .Net languages has been deprecated, and the replacement only compiles on Windows).
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
         <a href="#cite_note-85">
          [85]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Perl
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="KDE_Applications">
        KDE Applications
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=KDE&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: KDE Applications">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/KDE_Applications" title="KDE Applications">
        KDE Applications
       </a>
       like
       <a href="/wiki/Okular" title="Okular">
        Okular
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/KTorrent" title="KTorrent">
        KTorrent
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kexi" title="Kexi">
        Kexi
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/KDE_Partition_Manager" title="KDE Partition Manager">
        KDE Partition Manager
       </a>
       are built on top of KDE Frameworks. KDE applications can potentially be portable between operating systems and independent of a particular workspace or desktop environment. Some brands identify application suites built up from several applications, such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kdenetwork" title="Kdenetwork">
        KDE Network
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kdegraphics" title="Kdegraphics">
        KDE Graphics
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kdeutils" title="Kdeutils">
        KDE Utilities
       </a>
       . Some applications are part of the regular Software Compilation releases, others are part of Extragear and release to their own schedule.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="KDE_neon">
        KDE neon
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=KDE&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: KDE neon">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       KDE neon is a software repository that uses Ubuntu LTS as a core. It aims to provide the users with rapidly updated Qt and KDE software, while updating the rest of the OS components from the Ubuntu repositories at the normal pace.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KDE-neon_86-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-KDE-neon-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIO-neon_87-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-CIO-neon-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       KDE maintains that it is not a "KDE distribution," but rather an up-to-date archive of KDE and Qt packages.
      </p>
      <p>
       It is provided in User, and Developer editions.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="WikiToLearn">
        WikiToLearn
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=KDE&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: WikiToLearn">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/WikiToLearn" title="WikiToLearn">
        WikiToLearn
       </a>
       , abbreviated WTL, is one of KDE's newest and most unique endeavors. It is a wiki (based on
       <a href="/wiki/MediaWiki" title="MediaWiki">
        MediaWiki
       </a>
       , like Wikipedia) that provides a platform to create and share open source textbooks. The idea is to have a massive library of textbooks for anyone and everyone to use and create. Its roots lay in
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Milan" title="University of Milan">
        University of Milan
       </a>
       , where a group of physics majors wanted to share notes—then decided that it was for everyone and not just their internal friend group. They now are a fully-fledged KDE project with many universities backing it.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Collaborations_with_other_organizations">
        Collaborations with other organizations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=KDE&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Collaborations with other organizations">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Wikimedia">
        Wikimedia
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=KDE&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Wikimedia">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" role="presentation" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="415" data-file-width="759" height="22" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/40px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/60px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/80px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png 2x" width="40"/>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text plainlist">
         Wikinews has related news:
         <i>
          <b>
           <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikinews.org/wiki/Wikipedia_founder_Jimmy_Wales_announces_cooperation_between_KDE_Group_and_Wikimedia" title="wikinews:Wikipedia founder Jimmy Wales announces cooperation between KDE Group and Wikimedia">
            Wikipedia founder Jimmy Wales announces cooperation between KDE Group and Wikimedia
           </a>
          </b>
         </i>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Amarok_2_3_0.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="765" data-file-width="1137" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Amarok_2_3_0.png/220px-Amarok_2_3_0.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Amarok_2_3_0.png/330px-Amarok_2_3_0.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Amarok_2_3_0.png/440px-Amarok_2_3_0.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Amarok_2_3_0.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Amarok with information retrieved from Wikipedia.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On 23 June 2005, chairman of the
       <a href="/wiki/Wikimedia_Foundation" title="Wikimedia Foundation">
        Wikimedia Foundation
       </a>
       announced that the KDE community and the Wikimedia Foundation have begun efforts towards cooperation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
        <a href="#cite_note-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Fruits of that cooperation are
       <a href="/wiki/MediaWiki" title="MediaWiki">
        MediaWiki
       </a>
       syntax highlighting in
       <a href="/wiki/Kate_(text_editor)" title="Kate (text editor)">
        Kate
       </a>
       and accessing
       <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia" title="Wikipedia">
        Wikipedia
       </a>
       content within KDE applications, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Amarok_(software)" title="Amarok (software)">
        Amarok
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Marble_(software)" title="Marble (software)">
        Marble
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       On 4 April 2008, the
       <a href="/wiki/KDE_e.V." title="KDE e.V.">
        KDE e.V.
       </a>
       and
       <a class="extiw" href="https://meta.wikimedia.org/wiki/Wikimedia_Deutschland" title="m:Wikimedia Deutschland">
        Wikimedia Deutschland
       </a>
       opened shared offices in
       <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">
        Frankfurt
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In September 2009 KDE e.V. moved to shared offices with
       <a href="/wiki/Free_Software_Foundation_Europe" title="Free Software Foundation Europe">
        Free Software Foundation Europe
       </a>
       in Berlin.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fsfeoffice_90-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-fsfeoffice-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Free_Software_Foundation_Europe">
        Free Software Foundation Europe
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=KDE&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Free Software Foundation Europe">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In May 2006, KDE e.V. became an
       <i>
        Associate Member
       </i>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Free_Software_Foundation_Europe" title="Free Software Foundation Europe">
        Free Software Foundation Europe
       </a>
       (FSFE).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fsfeoffice_90-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-fsfeoffice-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 22 August 2008, KDE e.V. and FSFE jointly announced that after working with FSFE’s
       <i>
        Freedom Task Force
       </i>
       for one and a half years KDE adopts FSFE’s
       <i>
        Fiduciary Licence Agreement
       </i>
       . Using that, KDE developers can – on a voluntary basis – assign their copyrights to KDE e.V.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In September 2009, KDE e.V. and FSFE moved into shared offices in Berlin.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_enterprises">
        Commercial enterprises
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=KDE&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Commercial enterprises">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Several companies actively contribute to KDE, like
       <a href="/wiki/Collabora" title="Collabora">
        Collabora
       </a>
       , Erfrakon, Intevation GmbH,
       <a href="/wiki/Kolab" title="Kolab">
        Kolab
       </a>
       Konsortium, Klarälvdalens Datakonsult AB (KDAB),
       <a href="/wiki/Blue_Systems" title="Blue Systems">
        Blue Systems
       </a>
       , and KO GmbH.
      </p>
      <p>
       Nokia used
       <a href="/wiki/Calligra_Suite" title="Calligra Suite">
        Calligra Suite
       </a>
       as base for their
       <i>
        Office Viewer
       </i>
       application for
       <a href="/wiki/Maemo" title="Maemo">
        Maemo
       </a>
       /
       <a href="/wiki/MeeGo" title="MeeGo">
        MeeGo
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
       They have also been contracting KO GmbH to bring MS Office 2007 file format filters to Calligra.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
        <a href="#cite_note-94">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Nokia also employed several KDE developers directly – either to use KDE software for MeeGo (e.g.
       <i>
        KCal
       </i>
       )
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
        <a href="#cite_note-95">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
       or as sponsorship.
      </p>
      <p>
       The software development and consulting companies Intevation GmbH of Germany and the Swedish KDAB use Qt and KDE software – especially
       <a href="/wiki/Kontact" title="Kontact">
        Kontact
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Akonadi" title="Akonadi">
        Akonadi
       </a>
       for
       <a href="/wiki/Kolab" title="Kolab">
        Kolab
       </a>
       – for their services and products, therefore both employ KDE developers.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Others">
        Others
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=KDE&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Others">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       KDE participates in
       <a href="/wiki/Freedesktop.org" title="Freedesktop.org">
        freedesktop.org
       </a>
       , an effort to standardize Unix desktop interoperability.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2009 and 2011,
       <a href="/wiki/GNOME" title="GNOME">
        GNOME
       </a>
       and KDE co-hosted their conferences
       <a href="/wiki/Akademy" title="Akademy">
        Akademy
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/GNOME_Users_And_Developers_European_Conference" title="GNOME Users And Developers European Conference">
        GUADEC
       </a>
       under the
       <i>
        Desktop Summit
       </i>
       label.
      </p>
      <p>
       In December 2010 KDE e.V. became a licensee of the
       <a href="/wiki/Open_Invention_Network" title="Open Invention Network">
        Open Invention Network
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Many
       <a href="/wiki/Linux_distribution" title="Linux distribution">
        Linux distributions
       </a>
       and other free operating systems are involved in the development and distribution of the software, and are therefore also active in the KDE community. These include commercial distributors such as
       <a href="/wiki/SUSE" title="SUSE">
        SUSE
       </a>
       /
       <a href="/wiki/Novell" title="Novell">
        Novell
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
        <a href="#cite_note-97">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
       or Red Hat
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
        <a href="#cite_note-98">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but also government-funded non-commercial organizations such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Scientific_and_Technological_Research_Council_of_Turkey" title="Scientific and Technological Research Council of Turkey">
        Scientific and Technological Research Council of Turkey
       </a>
       with its Linux distribution Pardus.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_uses">
        Notable uses
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=KDE&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Notable uses">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Brazil’s primary school education system operates computers running KDE software, with more than 42,000 schools in 4,000 cities, thus serving nearly 52 million children. The base distribution is called Educational Linux, which is based on
       <a href="/wiki/Kubuntu" title="Kubuntu">
        Kubuntu
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
        <a href="#cite_note-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Besides this, thousands more students in Brazil use KDE products in their universities. KDE software is also running on computers in Portuguese and Venezuelan schools, with respectively 700,000 and one million systems reached.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
        <a href="#cite_note-100">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Germany uses KDE software in its embassies around the world, representing around 11,000 systems. Through use of
       <a href="/wiki/Pardus_(operating_system)" title="Pardus (operating system)">
        Pardus
       </a>
       , a local Linux distribution, many sections of the Turkish government make use of KDE software, including the
       <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Armed_Forces" title="Turkish Armed Forces">
        Turkish Armed Forces
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-radikal_101-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-radikal-101">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Turkey)" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Turkey)">
        Ministry of Foreign Affairs
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-radikal_101-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-radikal-101">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_National_Defence_(Turkey)" title="Ministry of National Defence (Turkey)">
        Ministry of National Defence
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
        <a href="#cite_note-102">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turkish_Police" title="Turkish Police">
        Turkish Police
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-radikal_101-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-radikal-101">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the SGK (Social Security Institution of Turkey),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-radikal_101-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-radikal-101">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
        <a href="#cite_note-103">
         [103]
        </a>
       </sup>
       although these departments often do not exclusively use Pardus as their operating system.
       <a href="/wiki/CERN" title="CERN">
        CERN
       </a>
       (European Organization for Nuclear Research) is using KDE software.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
        <a href="#cite_note-104">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The major U.S. based home improvement store chain
       <a href="/wiki/Lowe%27s" title="Lowe's">
        Lowe's
       </a>
       uses a version of OpenSuSE running KDE on the computers used by store associates.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
        <a href="#cite_note-105">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="KDE_Patrons">
        KDE Patrons
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=KDE&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: KDE Patrons">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       A KDE Patron pays from 5000 Euro (depending on the companies size).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
        <a href="#cite_note-106">
         [106]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As of May 2017 there are 5:
       <a href="/wiki/Blue_Systems" title="Blue Systems">
        Blue Systems
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canonical_Ltd." title="Canonical Ltd.">
        Canonical Ltd.
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">
        Google
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/SUSE" title="SUSE">
        SUSE
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/The_Qt_Company" title="The Qt Company">
        The Qt Company
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
        <a href="#cite_note-107">
         [107]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
